SECTION 5.04. Headings. The headings contained in this Agreement are for reference purposes only and shall not affect in any way the meaning or interpretation of this Agreement.

SECTION 5.05. Severability. If any term or other provision of this Agreement is invalid, illegal or incapable of being enforced by any applicable Law or public policy, all other conditions and provisions of this Agreement shall nevertheless remain in full force and effect so long as the economic or legal substance of the transactions contemplated hereby is not fundamentally changed. Upon such determination that any term or other provision is invalid, illegal or incapable of being enforced, the parties shall negotiate in good faith to modify this Agreement so as to effect the original intent of the parties as closely as possible in a mutually acceptable manner in order that the transactions contemplated hereby be consummated as originally contemplated to the greatest extent possible.

SECTION 5.06. Entire Agreement. This Agreement, together with the Acquisition Agreement, the other Ancillary Agreements and the Confidentiality Agreement, constitutes the entire agreement of the parties with respect to the subject matter hereof and supersedes all prior agreements and undertakings, both written and oral, between Seller and Purchaser with respect to the subject matter hereof.

SECTION 5.07. Acquisition Agreement. Neither the making nor the acceptance of this Agreement shall enlarge, restrict or otherwise modify the terms of the Acquisition Agreement or constitute a waiver or release by Seller or Purchaser of any liabilities, obligations or commitments imposed upon them by the terms of the Acquisition Agreement, including the representations, warranties, covenants, agreements and other provisions of the Acquisition Agreement. In the event of any conflict between the provisions of this Agreement (including Schedule A annexed hereto), on the one hand, and the provisions of the Acquisition Agreement, on the other hand, the Acquisition Agreement shall control.

 

10

SECTION 5.08. Assignment. Except as expressly specified in this Agreement, neither party may transfer any of its rights or obligations hereunder, without the prior written consent of the other party. Any assignment in violation of this Section 5.08 shall be null and void.

SECTION 5.09. No Third-Party Beneficiaries. This Agreement is for the sole benefit of the parties and their permitted assigns except for, in the case of Section 4.01 and Section 4.02(a), the Seller Indemnified Persons and, in the case of Section 4.02(b), the Purchaser Indemnified Persons, and nothing herein, express or implied, is intended to or shall confer upon any other Person any legal or equitable right, benefit or remedy of any nature whatsoever under or by reason of this Agreement.

SECTION 5.10. Amendment. This Agreement may not be amended or modified except by an instrument in writing signed by the parties hereto.

SECTION 5.11. Dispute Resolution. The Relationship Managers shall negotiate in good faith and attempt to resolve any disputes regarding this Agreement or the Services provided hereunder. If the Relationship Managers cannot resolve a dispute within two weeks after notification of the dispute, then either Purchaser or Seller may request that the issue be escalated to a senior executive from Purchaser and an executive officer from Seller who shall meet as promptly as practicable after receipt of a request to discuss a dispute, and shall cause information to be presented and will negotiate in good faith in an effort to resolve the dispute without the necessary of any formal proceedings related thereto. If the issue cannot be resolved by such senior executive officers without two weeks after the matter is referred to them, then it may be resolved in accordance with Section 5.12 and Section 5.14 of this Agreement.

SECTION 5.12. Governing Law; Submission to Jurisdiction. (a) This Agreement and any dispute arising out of or relating to or in connection with this Agreement shall be governed by, and construed in accordance with, the Laws of the State of New York.

(b) To the fullest extent permitted by applicable Law, each party hereto (i) agrees that any claim, action or proceeding by such party seeking any relief whatsoever arising out of, relating to or in connection with, this Agreement or the transactions contemplated hereby shall be brought only in the United States District Court for the Southern District of New York or in any New York State court, in each case, located in the Borough of Manhattan and not in any other State or Federal court in the United States of America or any court in any other country, (ii) agrees to submit to the exclusive jurisdiction of such courts located in the Borough of Manhattan for purposes of all legal proceedings arising out of, or in connection with, this Agreement or the transactions contemplated hereby, (iii) waives and agrees not to assert any objection that it may now or hereafter have to the laying of the venue of any such Action brought in such a court or any claim that any such Action brought in such a court has been brought in an inconvenient forum, (iv) agrees that mailing of process or other papers in connection with any such action or proceeding in the manner provided in Section 5.03 or any other manner as may be permitted by Law shall be valid and sufficient service thereof and (v) agrees that a final judgment in any such action or proceeding shall be conclusive and may be enforced in other jurisdictions by suit on the judgment or in any other manner provided by applicable Law.

 

11

SECTION 5.13. Counterparts. This Agreement may be executed in one or more counterparts, and by the different parties in separate counterparts, each of which when executed shall be deemed to be an original but all of which taken together shall constitute one and the same agreement. Delivery of an executed counterpart of a signature page to this Agreement by facsimile or other electronic means (including portable document format) shall be as effective as delivery of a manually executed counterpart of this Agreement.

SECTION 5.14. Waiver of Jury Trial. Each party hereby waives, to the fullest extent permitted by applicable Law, any right it may have to a trial by jury in respect to any litigation, directly or indirectly, arising out of or relating to this Agreement or any transaction contemplated by this Agreement. Each party (a) certifies that no representative, agent or attorney of any other party has represented, expressly or otherwise, that such other party would not, in the event of litigation, seek to enforce the foregoing waiver and (b) acknowledges that it and the other parties have been induced to enter into this Agreement by, among other things, the mutual waivers and certifications in this Section 5.14.

SECTION 5.15. No Set-off. Each party, on behalf of itself and each of its Affiliates, agrees that (a) its rights and remedies under this Agreement shall not give rise to any right of set-off, defense or counterclaim under the Acquisition Agreement or any Ancillary Agreement (other than this Agreement) and (b) any rights and remedies that it or any of its Affiliates may have under the Acquisition Agreement or any Ancillary Agreement (other than this Agreement) shall not give rise to any right it may have to set-off, defense or counterclaim under this Agreement.

SECTION 5.16. Taxes. The amount of any actual and documented sales tax, value added tax, goods and services tax or similar tax that is required to be paid by Seller or its Affiliates in connection with the Transition Services provided hereunder, will be promptly reimbursed to Seller by Purchaser, and such reimbursement shall be in addition to the amounts required to be paid to Seller under Section 2.02 unless such tax is already accounted for in Schedule A.

SECTION 5.17. Performance Guaranty. Guarantor hereby guarantees the performance and discharge by Seller of, and compliance by Seller with, all of the obligations, covenants, and undertakings of Seller under this Agreement in accordance with the terms hereof.

ARTICLE I – DEFINITIONS

(c) “Licensed Products” means those specific products or services sold by Licensee under particular Licensed Marks as of the Effective Date.

ARTICLE III – QUALITY CONTROL

Section 3.1 Quality Control. Licensee recognizes that Licensor has a reputation for high quality products. The nature and quality of Licensed Products sold in connection with the Licensed Marks shall be of high quality consistent with that of Licensor, and shall be at least as high a quality as, and with specifications consistent with, such Licensed Products that were sold by Licensee as of the Effective Date.

Section 3.2 Licensee’s Obligations of Compliance and Use.

(a) Licensee shall use and display the Licensed Marks only in such form and manner approved by Licensor pursuant to Section 4.1.

(b) Licensee recognizes that the distribution, sale and marketing of Licensed Products might affect the reputation of Licensor and the Licensed Marks. In connection with Licensee’s use of any of the Licensed Marks, Licensee shall at all times comply with any reasonable written trademark usage guidelines or any other reasonable related standards provided by Licensor to Licensee, as may be updated by Licensor from time to time.

(c) Licensee shall not intentionally or recklessly act in a manner likely to prejudice the validity, enforceability, fame or distinctiveness of any of the Licensed Marks. Licensee shall not intentionally or recklessly harm the goodwill associated with the Licensed Marks or take any action which it knows, or has reason to know, would threaten to injure the image or reputation of Licensor or the Licensed Marks, including, without limitation, advertising in any way which could damage the goodwill of the Licensed Marks.

(d) Licensee shall cause to appear on the Licensed Products and on their tags, packaging, advertising and promotional materials, such legends, markings and notices as Licensor may reasonably request, which, unless otherwise notified by Licensor, shall be set forth on Schedule C.

(e) From time to time, at Licensor’s request and for the purpose of verifying compliance with this Article III, Licensee shall provide samples of the Licensed Products and any other further information reasonably requested by Licensor for that purpose. If at any time Licensor is of the opinion that the quality of the Licensed Products does not meet the specified

 

3

quality standards, Licensor shall provide a notice to Licensee including an explanation of such deficiency and giving Licensee a reasonable period of time to effect the necessary changes to bring such Licensed Products within the specified quality standards and to resubmit the Licensed Products for approval. If Licensor fails to approve or disapprove a submission through Licensor’s standard review procedures generally applicable to licensees within forty-five (45) days after Licensor’s receipt of those materials necessary for its review, Licensor shall be deemed to have disapproved of such submission and Licensee shall have no right to use the Licensed Mark in connection therewith.

Section 3.3 Product Identification. Licensee shall ensure that each Licensed Product has an indelible, unique identifier in a manner that designates Licensee as the manufacturer of such Licensed Product. For illustrative purposes only, such an identifier could include a serial number.

ARTICLE IV – APPROVALS

Section 4.1 Approval Process.

(a) Licensee, at its expense, shall submit to Licensor all materials, including packaging (including user guides and other in-box materials), labeling, point of sale materials, public relations materials, trade show materials and displays, sales materials and advertising and promotional materials, bearing the Licensed Marks (“Materials”), and if such items are in a foreign language, translations of such items along with certification that such translations are accurate, for Licensor’s advance written approval, such approval not to be unreasonably withheld or delayed, prior to use, sale or distribution; provided that any Materials in use by Licensee as of the Effective Date shall be deemed approved by Licensor. If Licensor fails to approve or disapprove a submission through Licensor’s standard review procedures generally applicable to licensees within ten (10) days after Licensor’s receipt of those materials necessary for its review, Licensor shall be deemed to have disapproved of such submission and Licensee shall have no right to use the Licensed Mark in connection therewith; provided that if Licensee then resubmits such submission and materials, then if Licensor fails to approve or disapprove such submission through Licensor’s standard review procedures generally applicable to licensees within five (5) days after Licensor’s receipt of those materials necessary for its review, Licensor shall be deemed to have approved of such submission.

(b) Notwithstanding the generality of the foregoing, the following rules shall apply to the review and approval process:

(i) Licensor reserves the right to withdraw approval for an item if it departs from the approved sample, or if any quality, liability or safety issues with respect to an item are subsequently identified.

(ii) In the event of any modification or change in use or quality of any Materials submitted for approval, or the use of the Licensed Marks on such Materials or on the Licensed Products, whether during the approval process or after final approval has been granted, Licensee shall re-submit such Materials for approval.

(iii) Licensee shall disclose all sources for any artwork not supplied by Licensor.

This Intellectual Property License Agreement (the “Agreement”) is made as of             , 2012 (the “Effective Date”) by and between Motorola Mobility LLC, a Delaware limited liability company (“Mobility”), General Instrument Corporation, a Pennsylvania corporation (“GIC”), ARRIS Group, Inc., a Delaware corporation (“Arris,” and together with GIC, “Home”) and, solely with respect to Section 2.4 and ARTICLE III, Google Inc., a Delaware corporation (“Google”). ARTICLE I – DEFINITIONS

Section 1.1 Defined Terms. Capitalized terms used but not defined herein shall have the meanings set forth in the Acquisition Agreement. As used in this Agreement, the following terms shall have the following meanings:

(a) “Business” means the Motorola Home business, to the extent currently operated by Seller, the Company or the Company Subsidiaries, consisting of (i) the provision of the Services and (ii) the design, manufacture, distribution and sale of Products, in each case excluding the Overhead and Shared Services.

(b) “Change of Control” means with respect to any Person (i) the sale of all or substantially all of the ownership interests in such Person in a single transaction or a series of transactions to one or more third parties, (ii) any direct or indirect acquisition, consolidation or merger of such Person by, with or into any third party (that is not an Affiliate of such Person), or (iii) any other corporate transaction or series of transactions in which Control of such Person is directly or indirectly transferred to one or more third parties (that is not, prior to such change, reorganization or transaction, an Affiliate of such Person), including by transferring an excess of fifty percent (50%) of such Person’s voting power, shares or equity, through a merger, consolidation, tender offer or similar transaction, to one or more third parties (that is not, prior to such change, reorganization or transaction, an Affiliate of such Person).

(c) “Confidential Information” means any trade secret, know-how or other proprietary and confidential information (including, for the avoidance of doubt, any source code of Software) included the Licensed GIC Intellectual Property or Licensed Mobility Intellectual Property.

(d) “Consideration” has the meaning specified in Schedule 1.1(f).

(e) “Field of Use” means the field of the Business.

(f) “Licensable” means that a Party has the right to grant sublicenses to the other Party within the scope granted in Section 2.1 or Section 3.1, as applicable, without (i) the need to obtain consent of any Person, (ii) the relinquishment or forbearance of any right of the sublicensing Party under the applicable license and (iii) the payment of royalties or other consideration by the sublicensing Party to any Person. In the event that neither Party nor its Subsidiaries has the right to grant a license or sublicense of the scope set forth in Section 2.1 or Section 3.1 of any particular Intellectual Property, then the license granted in Section 2.1 or Section 3.1 under such Intellectual Property shall be of the broadest scope which such Party or its Subsidiary has the right to grant within the scope granted in Section 2.1 or Section 3.1.

(g) “Licensed GIC Intellectual Property” means (i) the Licensed GIC Patent Claims and (ii) any Software, copyright, trade secret, know-how or other Intellectual Property (other than Patents and Trademarks) that is used by the businesses of Mobility, Google or its Affiliates (other than the Company and its Subsidiaries) as of the Effective Date and owned or Licensable by GIC or its Subsidiaries as of the Effective Date.

(h) “Licensed GIC Patent Claims” means any claim of a Patent (i) owned or Licensable by GIC or its Subsidiaries as of the Effective Date, (ii) owned or Licensable by GIC or its Subsidiaries and that issues from a patent application that is filed by GIC or its Subsidiaries (or by an inventor who at the time of filing has an obligation to assign such application to GIC or its Subsidiaries) and is entitled to a priority date prior to the first (1st) anniversary of the Effective Date or (iii) which becomes owned or Licensable by GIC or its Subsidiaries pursuant to one or more Contracts with the entities listed on Schedule 1.1(h), irrespective of its filing or priority date; provided, that Licensed GIC Patent Claims exclude any claim of any Patent acquired by GIC or its Subsidiaries from a third-party after the Effective Date and any divisonals, continuations, continuations-in-part and all reissues, reexaminations, extensions, divisions and renewals thereof.

(i) “Licensed Mobility Intellectual Property” means (i) Licensed Mobility Patent Claims, (ii) Licensed Retained Patent Claims and (iii) any Software, copyright, trade secret, know-how or other Intellectual Property (other than Patents and Trademarks) that is used by the Business as of the Effective Date and owned or Licensable by Mobility or its Subsidiaries as of the Effective Date.

(j) “Licensed Mobility Patent Claims” means any claim of a Mobility Patent which is practiced by the making, using, offering to sell, selling or importing any current product or service of the Business. Licensed Mobility Patent Claims shall not include any Excluded Patent Claim (as defined in Schedule 1.1(j)) when practiced by or in connection with the Excluded Patent Claims Products (as defined in Schedule 1.1(j)).

 

2

(k) “Licensed Mobility Patent Products” means the current products and services of the Business and any extensions thereof that are within the Field of Use, but solely to the extent that such products, services and extensions are made by Home or its Affiliates or, in accordance with Section 2.3, by contractors of Home or its Affiliates; provided, however, that Licensed Mobility Patent Products excludes any laptops, smart phones, cell phones, tablet devices (other than tablet devices having a primary function of interaction with television that are not general-purpose tablets), eReaders and wearable devices, including glasses and watches.

(l) “Licensed Retained Patent Claims” means any claim of a Patent which is listed on Schedule 1.1(l).

(m) “Licensed Retained Products” means any products and services within the Field of Use, but solely to the extent that such products and services are made by Home or its Affiliates or, in accordance with Section 2.3, by contractors of Home or its Affiliates; provided, however, that Licensed Retained Products excludes any laptops, smart phones, cell phones, tablet devices (other than tablet devices having a primary function of interaction with television that are not general-purpose tablets), eReaders and wearable devices, including glasses and watches.

(n) “Mobility Patent” means any Patent (i) owned or Licensable by Mobility or its Subsidiaries (other than GIC or its Subsidiaries) as of the Effective Date, (ii) owned or Licensable by Mobility or its Subsidiaries (other than GIC or its Subsidiaries) and that issues from a patent application that is filed by Mobility or its Subsidiaries (other than GIC or its Subsidiaries) or by an inventor who at the time of filing has an obligation to assign such application to Mobility or its Subsidiaries (other than GIC or its Subsidiaries) and is entitled to a priority date prior to the first (1st) anniversary of the Effective Date or (iii) which becomes owned or Licensable by Mobility or its Subsidiaries pursuant to one or more Contracts with the entities listed on Schedule 1.1(n), irrespective of its filing or priority date; provided, however, that Mobility Patent specifically and without limitation excludes: (a) any Patent owned by Google Inc. or Google Inc.’s Subsidiaries (other than Mobility and its Subsidiaries); (b) any Patent which was Licensable by Google Inc. or any of Google Inc.’s Subsidiaries prior to May 22, 2012 except to the extent any such Patent was also owned or Licensable by Mobility or its Subsidiaries prior to such date; and (c) any Patent acquired by Mobility or its Subsidiaries from a third-party after the Effective Date and any divisonals, continuations, continuations-in-part and all reissues, reexaminations, extensions, divisions and renewals thereof.

(o) “Open Source Software” means any Software licensed under an “open source,” “copyleft,” or similar license that requires, as a condition of use, modification and/or distribution of any Software, that such Software, or any Software linked to, integrated with, derived from, used, or distributed with such Software or into which such Software is incorporated: (i) be made available or distributed in source code form, (ii) be licensed for the purpose of preparing derivative works, or (iii) be redistributable at no license fee. Copyleft licenses include, without limitation, the GNU General Public License, the GNU Lesser General Public License, and the Mozilla Public License.

(p) “Patents” means U.S. and foreign issued patents and patent applications, divisionals, continuations and continuations-in-part, and all reissues, reexaminations, extensions, divisions and renewals to any of the foregoing.

 

3

(q) “Software” means all computer programs and other software, including firmware and microcode, development tools and including software implementations of algorithms and software models and methodologies, whether in source code, object code or other form, including software libraries, subroutines and other components thereof.

ARTICLE II – LICENSE TO GIC

Section 2.1 License to GIC. Mobility, on behalf of itself and its Subsidiaries, grants to Home, in consideration for the Consideration, a non-exclusive, worldwide, irrevocable, perpetual, non-sublicenseable (other than pursuant to Section 2.2) and non-transferable (other than pursuant to Section 2.5) license under (i) the Licensed Retained Patent Claims to make, use, offer to sell, sell and import any Licensed Retained Products, (ii) the Licensed Mobility Patent Claims to make, use, offer to sell, sell and import any Licensed Mobility Patent Products, and (iii) the Licensed Mobility Intellectual Property (other than Patents) to use, copy, disclose, distribute, modify, display, publish, create derivative works of and otherwise commercially exploit such Licensed Mobility Intellectual Property in connection with any Licensed Retained Products.

Section 2.2 Sublicensing Rights. The rights granted in Section 2.1 include the right to grant sublicenses within the scope of the licenses granted in Section 2.1 solely to (i) Affiliates (other than joint ventures) of Arris (with the right to further sublicense pursuant to clause (ii) and (iii) below), provided that any right granted to an Affiliate of Arris hereunder shall terminate on the date such entity ceases to be an Affiliate of Arris; (ii) Home’s and its sublicensed Affiliates’ contractors, but only to the extent necessary for such contractor’s performances of services for Home in connection with the Licensed Retained Products (with respect to the license of Section 2.1(i)) or Licensed Mobility Patent Products (with respect to the license of Section 2.1(ii)) and (iii) Home’s customers and end users of Licensed Retained Products (with respect to the license of Section 2.1(i)) or Licensed Mobility Patent Products (with respect to the license of Section 2.1(ii)), but only for such customers’ and end users’ use of such products sold or provided by or on behalf of Home. Home shall be responsible and liable to Mobility in the event that any of its sublicensees fails to comply with any applicable provision of this Agreement.

Section 2.3 Have-made Right. The rights granted in Section 2.1 include the right of Home and its sublicensed Affiliates to have Licensed Retained Products (with respect to the license of Section 2.1(i)) or Licensed Mobility Patent Products (with respect to the license of Section 2.1(ii)) of Home’s or such Affiliates’ own design and specification made by one or more contractors solely for subsequent sale or distribution by Home or such Affiliates in its or their ordinary course of business; provided, that such right to have products made by one or more contractors shall not apply to (i) any products in the form manufactured or marketed by such contractor prior to Home’s or its Affiliates’ provision of such design and specification and (ii) any methods used by such contractor.

Section 2.4 Release. Google, on behalf of itself and its Subsidiaries (including Mobility), hereby fully and forever releases, acquits and discharges GIC and its current Subsidiaries, and any of their predecessors, successors, officers, employees, agents and representatives (“GIC Released Entities”) from any and all known and unknown claims, demands, liabilities, damages, suits, actions and causes of action relating to or arising out of any infringement or alleged infringement by GIC Released Entities of any Patent by making, using, offering to sell, selling and importing the current products and services of the Business that occurred prior to the Effective Date.

 

4

Section 2.5 Assignment and Change of Control.

(a) Neither GIC nor Arris may assign this Agreement or any of its rights or obligations hereunder, in whole or in part, to any Person without the prior written consent of Mobility. Notwithstanding the foregoing, subject to the restrictions set forth in Sections 2.5(b)-(e), Arris may (i) assign this Agreement and all of its rights and obligations hereunder in whole (but not in part), without Mobility’s consent, in connection with the sale of all or substantially all of its and its Subsidiaries’ assets, or GIC’s or its Subsidiaries’ assets, to which, at the time of such sale, the licenses granted under ARTICLE II pertain and (ii) assign this Agreement and its rights and obligations hereunder in part, without Mobility’s consent, in connection with the sale of a division of the Business with aggregate revenue (from the sale or provision of products and services included in such division) in excess of $100,000,000 in the full calendar year prior to such sale (a “Divested Entity”); provided that Arris may exercise its right to assign its rights and obligations hereunder in part pursuant to this clause (ii) only two (2) times (namely, in connection with the sale of two Divested Entities).

(b) Following a permitted assignment by Arris pursuant to Section 2.5(a)(i) or a Change of Control of Arris or GIC, any pre-existing or later acquired operations, businesses, products, product lines or services of the acquiring party shall not be licensed pursuant to this Agreement under any Licensed Mobility Intellectual Property (irrespective of whether or not they constitute Licensed Retained Products or Licensed Mobility Patent Products).

(c) Following a permitted assignment by Arris pursuant to Section 2.5(a)(ii), (i) any pre-existing or later acquired operations, businesses, products, product lines or services of the party acquiring the Divested Entity and its Affiliates shall not be licensed pursuant to this Agreement under any Licensed Mobility Intellectual Property (irrespective of whether or not they constitute Licensed Retained Products or Licensed Mobility Patent Products), (ii) “Licensed Mobility Patent Products” and “Licensed Retained Products” for purposes of the license rights assigned pursuant to Section 2.5(a)(ii) shall be limited to only those products and services manufactured, offered for sale, sold or imported by the relevant Divested Entity at the time of its sale and extensions thereof that are within the field of the relevant Divested Entity which field shall be, for the avoidance of doubt, no broader than the Field of Use; and in each case limited further to only such products and services made by the Divested Entity or, in accordance with Section 2.3, by contractors of the Divested Entity, (iii) all license rights assigned pursuant to Section 2.5(a)(ii) will automatically terminate on the date when the operations of the relevant Divested Entity are integrated with the acquiring party’s other business or product lines or the Divested Entity otherwise ceases to operate as an independent entity or division, (iv) the assignee pursuant to Section 2.5(a)(ii) shall have no right to further assign the rights and obligations assigned to it under this Agreement in whole or in part and (v) [Argon], GIC and their Subsidiaries shall retain no rights or licenses with respect to any product or service categories of the products and services of the Divested Entity at the time of its sale.

 

5

(d) As a condition to any assignment or Change of Control which is permitted under this Section 2.5, (i) Arris shall provide written notice to Mobility identifying the assignee or acquirer of Control and, in the case of assignment pursuant to Section 2.5(a)(ii), the Divested Entity and its products and services, (ii) such assignee or acquiring party shall agree in writing to assume all applicable obligations of Home hereunder and, with respect to any Licensed GIC Intellectual Property assigned to or acquired by such assignee or acquiring party, under the license of Section 3.1 and (iii) Home shall not be relieved of any of its accrued obligations hereunder.

(e) Notwithstanding anything to the contrary in this Section 2.5, upon a Change of Control or sale of all or substantially all of the assets of GIC (independent of a Change of Control or sale of all or substantially all of the assets of Arris), Arris shall elect either (i) to retain all rights granted under this ARTICLE II (in which case all rights granted under this ARTICLE II to GIC and its Subsidiaries shall automatically terminate upon such Change of Control or sale and Arris shall not have the right pursuant to Section 2.5(a) to assign this Agreement and the rights and obligations hereunder to the party acquiring such assets or control) or (ii) to assign this Agreement and all of its rights and obligations hereunder in whole (but not in part) to the party acquiring such assets or control (in which case all right grants under this ARTICLE II to Arris and its Subsidiaries (other than GIC and its Subsidiaries) shall automatically terminate upon such Change of Control or sale).

(f) Any attempted assignment in violation of this Section 2.5 shall be void and of no effect.

ARTICLE III – LICENSE-BACK TO MOBILITY

Section 3.1 License-back to Mobility. GIC, on behalf of itself and its Subsidiaries, grants to Mobility and Google, in consideration for the Consideration, a non-exclusive, worldwide, irrevocable, perpetual, non-sublicenseable (other than pursuant to Section 3.2) and non-transferable (other than pursuant to Section 3.5) license (i) under the Licensed GIC Patent Claims to make, use, offer to sell, sell and import any products and services and practice any methods in connection therewith and (ii) to use, copy, disclose, distribute, modify, display, publish, create derivative works of and otherwise commercially exploit the Licensed GIC Intellectual Property (other than Patents) in connection with products and services within the fields of the businesses of Mobility, Google and their Affiliates.

Section 3.2 Sublicensing Rights. The rights granted in Section 3.1 include the right to grant sublicenses, within the scope of the license granted in Section 3.1, solely to (i) Affiliates of Mobility and Google (with the right to further sublicense pursuant to clauses (ii) and (iii) below), provided that any right granted to an Affiliate hereunder shall terminate on the date such entity ceases to be an Affiliate of Mobility and Google; (ii) Mobility’s, Google’s and their sublicensed Affiliates’ (x) contractors, but only to the extent necessary for such contractor’s performances of services for Mobility, Google or such Affiliates in connection with products and services made by Mobility, Google or such Affiliates or, in accordance with Section 3.3, by their contractors or (y) original design manufacturers (“ODMs”), to the extent necessary for such ODMs to manufacture for, and sell and import to, Mobility, Google or their Affiliates products manufactured and/or designed (in whole or in part) by such ODMs for subsequent

 

6

commercialization by or on behalf of Mobility, Google or their Affiliates and (iii) customers and end users of the products and services referenced in the foregoing clauses (ii)(x) and (ii)(y), but only to the extent necessary for such customers’ and end users’ use of products and services sold or provided by or on behalf of Mobility, Google or such Affiliates, as such products and services are intended to be used. Mobility and Google shall be responsible and liable to Home in the event that any of its sublicensees fails to comply with any applicable provision of this Agreement.

Section 3.3 Have-made Right. The rights granted in Section 3.1 include the right of Mobility and Google to have products and services of Mobility’s, Google’s or its Affiliates’ own design and specification made by one or more contractors solely for subsequent sale or distribution by Mobility, Google or its Affiliates in its ordinary course of business; provided, that such right to have products or services made by one or more contractors shall not apply to (i) any products in the form manufactured or marketed by such contractor prior to Mobility’s, Google’s or its Affiliates’ provision of such design and specification or (ii) any methods used by such contractor.

Section 3.4 Release. Home hereby fully and forever releases, acquits and discharges Mobility, Google and their Affiliates, and any of their predecessors, successors, officers, employees, agents and representatives (“Mobility Released Entities”) from any and all known and unknown claims, demands, liabilities, damages, suits, actions and causes of action relating to or arising out of any infringement or alleged infringement by Mobility Released Entities of any Licensed GIC Patent Claim by making, using, offering to sell, selling and importing any product or service that occurred prior to the Effective Date, but only to the extent such activity would have been covered by the license of Section 3.1 if such activity occurred after the Effective Date.

Section 3.5 Assignment and Change of Control.

(a) Neither Mobility nor Google may assign this Agreement or any of its rights or obligations hereunder, in whole or in part, to any Person without the prior written consent of Arris. Notwithstanding the foregoing, subject to the restrictions set forth in Section 3.5(b)-Section 3.5(d), Google or Mobility (but not both) may (i) assign this Agreement and all of its or their rights and obligations hereunder in whole (but not in part), without Arris’s consent, in connection with the sale of all or substantially all of their and their Subsidiaries’ assets to which, at the time of such sale, the licenses granted under ARTICLE III pertain, and (ii) assign this Agreement and their rights and obligations hereunder in part, without Arris’s consent, in connection with the sale of a business division with aggregate revenue (from the sale or provision of products and services included in such division) in excess of $100,000,000 in the full calendar year prior to such sale (a “Mobility Divested Entity”); provided that Mobility and Google may exercise the right to assign rights and obligations hereunder in part pursuant to this clause (ii) only two (2) times (namely, in connection with the sale of two Mobility Divested Entities).

(b) Following a permitted assignment by Mobility or Google pursuant to Section 3.5(a) or a Change of Control of Mobility or Google, any pre-existing or later acquired operations, businesses, products, product lines or services of the acquiring party shall not be licensed pursuant to this Agreement under any Licensed GIC Intellectual Property.

 

7

(c) Following a permitted assignment pursuant to Section 2.5(a)(ii), (i) any pre-existing or later acquired operations, businesses, products, product lines or services of the party acquiring the Mobility Divested Entity and its Affiliates shall not be licensed pursuant to this Agreement under any Licensed GIC Intellectual Property, (ii) the licensed products and services for purposes of the license rights assigned pursuant to Section 2.5(a)(ii) shall be limited to only those products and services within the field of the relevant Mobility Divested Entity and limited further to only such products and services made by the Mobility Divested Entity or, in accordance with Section 2.3, by contractors of the Mobility Divested Entity, (iii) all license rights assigned pursuant to Section 2.5(a)(ii) will automatically terminate on the date when the operations of the relevant Mobility Divested Entity are integrated with the acquiring party’s other business or product lines or the Mobility Divested Entity otherwise ceases to operate as an independent entity or division, (iv) the assignee pursuant to Section 2.5(a)(ii) shall have no right to further assign the rights and obligations assigned to it under this Agreement in whole or in part and (v) Google, Mobility and their Subsidiaries shall retain no rights or licenses with respect to any product or service categories of the products and services of the Mobility Divested Entity at the time of its sale.

(d) As a condition to any assignment or Change of Control which is permitted under this Section 3.5, (i) Mobility shall provide written notice to Arris identifying the assignee or acquirer of Control and, in the case of assignment pursuant to Section 3.5(a)(ii), the Mobility Divested Entity and its products and services, (ii) such assignee or acquirer shall agree in writing to assume all applicable obligations of Mobility or Google, as applicable, hereunder and, with respect to any Licensed Mobility Intellectual Property assigned to or acquired by such assignee or acquirer, under the license of Section 3.1, and (iii) Mobility or Google, as applicable, shall not be relieved of any of its accrued obligations hereunder.

(e) Any attempted assignment in violation of this Section 3.5 shall be void and of no effect.

Section 4.1 Reservation of Rights. Except as expressly provided hereunder, each Party reserves all rights to its Intellectual Property not expressly granted in this Agreement, and no license is granted herein, either directly or by implication, estoppel or otherwise under this Agreement with respect to any Patents, other than as expressly provided in Section 2.1 and Section 3.1. No assignment or transfer of any right, title or ownership interest to any Party’s Intellectual Property is conveyed pursuant to this Agreement.

Section 4.2 WARRANTY DISCLAIMER. ALL OF THE RIGHTS PROVIDED HEREUNDER ARE PROVIDED ON AN AS-IS, WHERE-IS BASIS, WITHOUT ANY REPRESENTATION OR WARRANTIES, WHETHER EXPRESS OR IMPLIED, INCLUDING ANY WARRANTY OF MERCHANTABILITY, NON-INFRINGEMENT OF THIRD PERSON INTELLECTUAL PROPERTY RIGHTS, OR FITNESS FOR A PARTICULAR PURPOSE, ALL OF WHICH ARE HEREBY DISCLAIMED.

 

8

Section 4.3 LIMITATION OF LIABILTY. UNDER NO CIRCUMSTANCES SHALL ANY PARTY HEREUNDER BE LIABLE FOR ANY CONSEQUENTIAL, SPECIAL, INDIRECT, INCIDENTAL OR PUNITIVE DAMAGES WHATSOEVER (INCLUDING, WITHOUT LIMITATION, DAMAGES FOR LOSS OF BUSINESS PROFITS, BUSINESS INTERRUPTION, LOSS OF BUSINESS INFORMATION, LOSS OF DATA OR OTHER PECUNIARY LOSS) ARISING OUT OF THE USE OF EITHER PARTY’S INTELLECTUAL PROPERTY OR THE RIGHTS GRANTED HEREUNDER, EVEN IF A PARTY HAS BEEN ADVISED OF THE POSSIBILITY OF SUCH DAMAGES. NO PARTY SHALL HAVE ANY OBLIGATION HEREUNDER TO INSTITUTE ANY ACTION OR SUIT AGAINST THIRD PARTIES FOR INFRINGEMENT OF ANY OF ITS INTELLECTUAL PROPERTY RIGHTS OR TO DEFEND ANY ACTION OR SUIT BROUGHT BY A THIRD PARTY WHICH CHALLENGES OR CONCERNS ANY OF ITS INTELLECTUAL PROPERTY RIGHTS.

Section 4.4 Disclaimer. None of the Parties shall be liable under this Agreement for any claims, loss or damages arising from any other Party’s or the other Party’s sublicensees’ use of any Patents licensed to such other Party or such sublicensees under this Agreement.

Section 4.5 Acquisition Agreement. Section 4.2 and Section 4.3 are not intended to supersede or nullify any representations, warranties, rights or remedies provided under the Acquisition Agreement, which shall be solely governed by the terms thereof.

Section 4.6 Prosecution, Maintenance and Enforcement. Nothing contained in this Agreement shall be construed as requiring the filing of any patent application, the securing of any Patent, or the maintaining of any Patent in force. No Party shall have any obligation hereunder to institute any action or suit against third parties for infringement of any of its Patents or to defend any action or suit brought by a third person which challenges or concerns any of its Patents.

Section 4.7 No Delivery or Support. Nothing in this Agreement shall be construed to require any delivery of any physical devices, Software, source code, object code, documentation or other tangible items by Mobility, Google or its Affiliates to Home or by Home to Mobility, Google or its Affiliates, or to require any support or maintenance obligations whatsoever on the part of either Party.

ARTICLE V – TERM AND TERMINATION

Section 5.1 Term. This Agreement and the rights and licenses granted and retained hereunder shall become effective on the Effective Date and shall continue thereafter perpetually.

ARTICLE VI – CONFIDENTIAL INFORMATION

Section 6.1 Obligation. The Parties shall use, at a minimum, the same degree of care as such Party uses to protect its own confidential information of a similar nature, but no less than reasonable care, to prevent the unauthorized use, disclosure or publication of Confidential Information.

Section 6.2 Exclusions. Notwithstanding the foregoing Section 6.1, no Party shall be bound by obligations restricting disclosure set forth in this Agreement with respect to any Confidential Information which: (i) lawfully becomes publicly available other than through a breach of this Agreement or any other confidentiality obligation on behalf of any third party; (ii)

 

9

was disclosed to such Party by a third party provided such third party, or any other party from whom such third party receives such information, is not in breach of any confidentiality obligation in respect of such information; (iii) is independently developed by such Party; or (iv) is disclosed when such disclosure is compelled pursuant to legal, judicial, or administrative proceedings, or otherwise required by law, court or governmental or regulatory authority, but solely to the extent required thereby.

ARTICLE VII – MISCELLANEOUS

Section 7.1 Waiver. Either Party may (a) extend the time for the performance of any of the obligations or other acts of the other Party or (b) waive compliance with any of the agreements or conditions contained herein. Any such extension or waiver shall be valid only if set forth in an instrument in writing signed by the Party to be bound thereby. Any failure to assert, or delay in the assertion of, rights under this Agreement shall not constitute a waiver of those rights.

Section 7.2 Expenses. Except as otherwise provided in this Agreement, the Parties shall bear their respective direct and indirect costs and expenses incurred in connection with the negotiation, preparation, execution and performance of this Agreement and the transactions contemplated hereby.

Section 7.3 Severability. If any term or other provision of this Agreement is invalid, illegal or incapable of being enforced by any applicable Law or public policy, all other conditions and provisions of this Agreement shall nevertheless remain in full force and effect, so long as the economic or legal substance of the transactions contemplated hereby is not fundamentally changed. Upon such determination that any term or other provision is invalid, illegal or incapable of being enforced, the Parties shall negotiate in good faith to modify this Agreement so as to effect the original intent of the Parties as closely as possible in a mutually acceptable manner in order for the transactions contemplated hereby to be consummated as originally contemplated to the greatest extent possible.

Section 7.4 Notices. All notices, submissions, confirmations, reports and statements to be given hereunder shall be given or made at the respective address of the Parties as set forth below, unless notification of a change of address is given in writing, and shall be sent by both generally recognized overnight courier service and confirmed facsimile transmission and shall be deemed to have been given when received.

Section 7.5 Entire Agreement. This Agreement, together with the Acquisition Agreement and the other Ancillary Agreements, constitutes the entire agreement of the Parties with respect to the subject matter hereof and supersedes all prior agreements and undertakings, both written and oral, between the Parties with respect to the subject matter hereof.

 

10

Section 7.6 Amendment. This Agreement may not be amended or modified except by an instrument in writing signed by Mobility and GIC.

Section 7.7 Governing Law; Jurisdiction; Waiver of Jury.

(a) This Agreement and any dispute arising out of or relating to or in connection with this Agreement shall be governed by, and construed in accordance with, the Laws of the State of New York.

(b) Subject to Section 7.8, to the fullest extent permitted by applicable Law, each Party hereto (i) agrees that any claim, action or proceeding by such Party seeking any relief whatsoever arising out of, relating to or in connection with, this Agreement or the transactions contemplated hereby shall be brought only in the United States District Court for the Southern District of New York or in any New York State court, in each case, located in the Borough of Manhattan and not in any other State or Federal court in the United States of America or any court in any other country, (ii) agrees to submit to the exclusive jurisdiction of such courts located in the Borough of Manhattan for purposes of all legal proceedings arising out of, or in connection with, this Agreement or the transactions contemplated hereby, (iii) waives and agrees not to assert any objection that it may now or hereafter have to the laying of the venue of any such Action brought in such a court or any claim that any such Action brought in such a court has been brought in an inconvenient forum, (iv) agrees that mailing of process or other papers in connection with any such action or proceeding in the manner provided in Section 11.03 of the Acquisition Agreement or any other manner as may be permitted by Law shall be valid and sufficient service thereof and (v) agrees that a final judgment in any such action or proceeding shall be conclusive and may be enforced in other jurisdictions by suit on the judgment or in any other manner provided by applicable Law.

(c) Each Party hereby waives, to the fullest extent permitted by applicable Law, any right it may have to a trial by jury in respect to any litigation, directly or indirectly, arising out of or relating to this Agreement or any transaction contemplated by this Agreement. Each Party (i) certifies that no representative, agent or attorney of the other Party has represented, expressly or otherwise, that such other Party would not, in the event of litigation, seek to enforce the foregoing waiver and (ii) acknowledges that the Parties have been induced to enter into this Agreement by, among other things, the mutual waivers and certifications in this Section 7.7.

Section 7.8 Resolution of Conflicts; Arbitration.

(a) Prior to commencing any arbitration under this Agreement, the Party desiring to commence the proceeding shall deliver notice to the other Party setting forth the nature of the dispute, and request a meeting of senior executives in order to settle the dispute in good faith (“Pre-arbitration Notice”). Within ten (10) days of delivery of the Pre-arbitration Notice, both Parties shall designate at least one senior executive (Vice President or higher) having authority to settle such disputes to meet and discuss the dispute with the other Party. The executives shall promptly meet at a mutually agreeable location and attempt to resolve the dispute in good faith within thirty (30) days from the date of delivery of the Pre-arbitration Notice. In the event the dispute is not settled within the thirty-day period, either Party may file an arbitration request under Section 7.8(b).

 

11

(b) Any claim or dispute arising out of or related to this Agreement, or the interpretation, making, performance, breach or termination thereof, shall (after compliance with Section 7.8(a)) be finally settled by binding and confidential arbitration administered by the American Arbitration Association in the County of Santa Clara, California in accordance with the then current Commercial Arbitration Rules of the American Arbitration Association and judgment upon the award rendered may be entered in any court having jurisdiction thereof. The arbitrator(s) shall have the authority to grant any equitable and legal remedies that would be available in any judicial proceeding instituted to resolve a dispute.

(c) Such arbitration shall be conducted by a single arbitrator chosen by mutual agreement of the Parties. Alternatively, at the request of either Party before the commencement of arbitration, the arbitration shall be conducted by three independent arbitrators, none of whom shall have any competitive interests with either of the Parties. Each Party shall each select one arbitrator. The two arbitrators so selected shall select a third arbitrator.

(d) In any arbitration under this Section 7.8, each Party shall be limited to calling a total of three witnesses both for purposes of deposition and the arbitration hearing. Subject to the foregoing limitation on the number of witnesses, the arbitrator or arbitrators, as the case may be, shall set a limited time period and establish procedures designed to reduce the cost and time for discovery while allowing the Parties an opportunity, adequate in the sole judgment of the arbitrator or majority of the three arbitrators, as the case may be, to discover relevant information from the opposing Party about the subject matter of the dispute. The arbitrator, or a majority of the three arbitrators, as the case may be, shall rule upon motions to compel or limit discovery and shall have the authority to impose sanctions for discovery abuses, including attorneys’ fees and costs, to the same extent as a competent court of law or equity, should the arbitrators or a majority of the three arbitrators, as the case may be, determine that discovery was sought without substantial justification or that discovery was refused or objected to without substantial justification.

(e) The decision of the arbitrator or a majority of the three arbitrators, as the case may be, as to any claim or dispute shall be final, binding, confidential, and conclusive upon the Parties to this Agreement. Such decision shall be written and shall be supported by written findings of fact and conclusions which shall set forth the award, judgment, decree or order awarded by the arbitrator(s). Within thirty (30) days of a decision of the arbitrator(s) requiring payment by one Party to another, such Party shall make the payment to such other Party.

(f) By agreeing to arbitration, the Parties do not intend to deprive any court of competent jurisdiction of its ability to issue any form of provisional remedy, including but not limited to a preliminary injunction, or order any interim or conservatory measure. A request for such provisional remedy or interim or conservatory measure by a Party to a court shall not be deemed a waiver of this agreement to arbitrate.

(g) The Parties agree that each Party shall pay its own costs and expenses (including counsel fees) of any such arbitration, and each Party waives its right to seek an order compelling the other Party to pay its portion of its costs and expenses (including counsel fees) for any arbitration.

 

12

(h) Notwithstanding anything to the contrary herein, the arbitration provisions set forth herein, and any arbitration conducted thereunder, shall be governed exclusively by the Federal Arbitration Act, Title 9 United States Code, to the exclusion of any state or municipal law of arbitration.

(i) Except as may be required by applicable law or court order, the Parties agree to maintain confidentiality as to all aspects of any arbitration, including its existence and results, except that nothing herein shall prevent any Party from disclosing information regarding such arbitration for purposes of proceedings to enforce this clause or to enforce the award or for purposes of seeking provisional remedies from a court of competent jurisdiction. The Parties further agree to obtain the arbitrators’ agreement to preserve the confidentiality of any arbitration.

Section 7.9 Availability of Equitable Relief. In the event of any breach or threatened breach by either Party of its obligations under this Agreement, the other Party shall be entitled to equitable relief (including specific performance) without prejudice to any other rights or remedies that may otherwise be available to such other Party.

Section 7.10 No Third Party Beneficiaries. This Agreement shall be binding upon and inure solely to the benefit of each Party hereto and its successors and permitted assigns and (to the extent set forth herein) its Subsidiaries and their successors and permitted assigns, and nothing in this Agreement is intended to or shall confer upon any other Person any legal or equitable rights, benefits or remedies of any nature whatsoever under or by reason of this Agreement.

Section 7.11 No Presumption. The Parties agree that this Agreement was negotiated fairly between them at arm’s length and that the final terms of this Agreement are the product of the Parties’ negotiations. Each Party represents and warrants that it has sought and received legal counsel of its own choosing with regard to the contents of this Agreement and the rights and obligations affected hereby. The Parties agree that this Agreement shall be deemed to have been jointly and equally drafted by them, and that the provisions of this Agreement therefore should not be construed against a Party on the grounds that the Party drafted or was more responsible for drafting the provisions.

Section 7.12 No Disclosure of Schedules. The Schedules to this Agreement are strictly confidential and shall not be disclosed to any Person or made publicly available other than as required to be disclosed pursuant to an applicable law, rule, regulation, self- regulation, government requirement, court order, the rules of any stock exchange or regulatory authority (provided, however, that the disclosing Party shall advise the other Party of such required disclosure promptly upon learning thereof in order to afford such other Party a reasonable opportunity to contest, limit and/or assist the disclosing Party in avoiding or crafting such disclosure).

 

13

Section 7.13 Headings. The headings contained in this Agreement are for reference purposes only and shall not affect in any way the meaning or interpretation of this Agreement.

Section 7.14 Counterparts. This Agreement may be executed in one or more counterparts, and by the different Parties in separate counterparts, each of which when executed shall be deemed to be an original but all of which taken together shall constitute one and the same agreement. Delivery of an executed counterpart of a signature page to this Agreement by facsimile or other electronic means (including portable document format) shall be as effective as delivery of a manually executed counterpart of this Agreement.
